  <meta property="og:title" content="CDC Issues Nationwide Alert After Hepatitis Outbreak Of Unknown Origin">
  <meta property="og:description" content="The Centers for Disease Control &amp; Prevention has issued a national alert to doctors over a mystery hepatitis outbreak.The CDC notified clinicians and public health authorities on Thursday, April 21 about a cluster of children identifie…">

  <script type="application/ld+json">
    {
      "@context": "http://schema.org",
      "@type": "NewsArticle",
      "articleBody": "The Centers for Disease Control &amp; Prevention has issued a national alert to doctors over a mystery hepatitis outbreak. \nThe CDC notified clinicians and public health authorities on Thursday, April 21 about a cluster of children identified with hepatitis and adenovirus infection, asking all physicians to be on the lookout for symptoms and to report any suspected cases of hepatitis of unknown origin to their local and state health departments. \nThe CDC said it is currently working with the Alabama Department of Public Health to investigate a cluster of nine cases of hepatitis of unknown origin in children ranging in age from 1 to 6 years old, all of whom were previously healthy.&nbsp; \nThe CDC said it's also working with state health departments to see if there are additional US cases, and what may be causing these cases.&nbsp; \n\"At this time, we believe adenovirus may be the cause for these reported cases, but investigators are still learning more \u2013 including ruling out other possible causes and identifying other possible contributing factors,\" the CDC said. \nThere has also been an increase in cases of pediatric hepatitis without a known cause recently reported in Europe and the CDC said it \"has been in contact with our European counterparts to understand what they are learning.\" \nAdenovirus has been confirmed in several of the European cases, but not all, the CDC said. \nSymptoms of hepatitis, or inflammation of the liver, include: \n\nfever,&nbsp;\nfatigue,&nbsp;\nloss of appetite,&nbsp;\nnausea,&nbsp;\nvomiting,&nbsp;\nabdominal pain,&nbsp;\ndark urine,&nbsp;\nlight-colored stools,&nbsp;\njoint pain,\njaundice\nAdenoviruses spread from person-to-person and most commonly cause respiratory illness, but depending on the type, can also cause other illnesses such as gastroenteritis (inflammation of the stomach or intestines), conjunctivitis (pink eye), and cystitis (bladder infection).&nbsp; \nAdenovirus type 41 typically presents as diarrhea, vomiting and fever, often accompanied by respiratory symptoms.&nbsp; \nCDC is asking physicians to consider adenovirus testing for pediatric patients with hepatitis of unknown etiology, and to report any possible cases of hepatitis of unknown origin to CDC and state public health authorities. \n\"In addition, we encourage parents and caregivers to be aware of the symptoms of hepatitis, and to contact their healthcare provider with any concerns,\" the CDC said.&nbsp; \nThe CDC said it's also recommending children be up to date on all their vaccinations, and that \"parents and caregivers of young children take the same everyday preventive actions that we recommend for everyone,\" including: \n\nWashing hands often,&nbsp;\nAvoiding people who are sick,&nbsp;\nCovering coughs and sneezes,&nbsp;\nAvoiding touching the eyes, nose or mouth.&nbsp;\nClick here to read the CDC alert. ",

  <article class="e-article" js-article-content="" data-testid="article-card">

    

    <header class="e-article-header">

      

      
      <h1 class="e-article-title" js-article-title="" data-testid="article-preview-title">
        
          CDC Issues Nationwide Alert After Hepatitis Outbreak Of Unknown Origin
        
        
      </h1>
    </header>

    
      
        <p>The Centers for Disease Control &amp; Prevention has issued a national alert to doctors over a mystery hepatitis outbreak.</p>
      
      
        


  

  <div class="b-article-detail-assets">
    
      
        


  
    <figure class="e-main-article-image">
      

      <picture class="e-media-container">
        
          
            <source media="(min-width: 768px)" srcset="https://edge.dailyvoice.com/cloudinary/Screenshot_2022-04-22_at_7.58.29_AM_czlfbr?width=1440&amp;height=720">
          
        
          
        
        <img class="e-media-image" itemprop="image" alt="Hepatitis" src="https://edge.dailyvoice.com/cloudinary/Screenshot_2022-04-22_at_7.58.29_AM_czlfbr?width=720&amp;height=360" js-article-image="">
      </picture>

      

      <figcaption class="e-media-info">
        
          <span class="e-media-caption" data-testid="article-preview-asset-caption">
            
              <p>Hepatitis</p>
            
          </span>
        
        
          <span class="e-media-credit">
            Photo Credit: <em class="e-credit-name" data-testid="article-preview-asset-credit">CDC</em>
          </span>
        
      </figcaption>

    </figure>
  


      
    
  </div>


      
    

    <section class="e-article-info">

      


<div class="b-bylines">
  <div class="e-byline">
    
      
        <a class="e-writer-img-link" js-byline-link="" href="/new-york/somers/staff/21/joe-lombardi/" rel="nofollow">
          
            <img class="e-writer-img" src="https://edge.dailyvoice.com/cloudinary/jlhed_qlrhlg?width=80&amp;height=80" width="40" height="40">
          
        </a>
      
      <a class="e-article-writer-link" js-byline-link="" data-testid="article-author" href="/new-york/somers/staff/21/joe-lombardi/" rel="nofollow">
        Joe Lombardi</a>
    

    
      


  <div class="b-article-user-social-links ">
    <div class="e-links">
      
        
          <a class="e-writer-social-link" data-testid="authors-social-links" href="https://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=728130222" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" title="Follow on Facebook">

              <span class="e-link-text">Facebook</span>
            
          </a>
        
      
        
          <a class="e-writer-social-link" data-testid="authors-social-links" href="https://twitter.com/joe_lombardi" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" title="@joe_lombardi">
            <i class="b-icon m-icon-twitter m-icon-xxsmall"></i>
            
              <span class="e-link-text">@joe_lombardi</span>
            
          </a>

      </a>
    </div>

    <button class="b-btn m-btn-icon m-btn-follow m-mobile-only" type="button" js-mobile-follow-btn="">
      <i class="b-icon m-icon-plus-outline m-icon-small"></i>
    </button>
  </div>


    
  </div>

</div>


      
        


<time data-testid="article-date" class="b-timestamp m-article-timestamp">
  
    04/22/2022 8:00 a.m.
  

</time>

      

      
    </section>


    <section class="e-article-body" js-article-body="">
      <div class="e-article-text" data-testid="article-detail-body" js-article-text="" data-read-smore-words="300">

        

        
          <p></p><p>The CDC notified clinicians and public health authorities on Thursday, April 21 about a cluster of children identified with hepatitis and adenovirus infection, asking all physicians to be on the lookout for symptoms and to report any suspected cases of hepatitis of unknown origin to their local and state health departments.</p><div class="e-instream-video-container" js-instream-video-container=""></div><p>The CDC said it is currently working with the Alabama Department of Public Health to investigate a cluster of nine cases of hepatitis of unknown origin in children ranging in age from 1 to 6 years old, all of whom were previously healthy.&nbsp;</p><div class="b-banner m-mobile-rectangle" data-position="mobile_rectangle" data-testid="mobile_rectangle" js-banner=""></div>
<p>The CDC said it's also working with state health departments to see if there are additional US cases, and what may be causing these cases.&nbsp;</p><p>"At this time, we believe adenovirus may be the cause for these reported cases, but investigators are still learning more – including ruling out other possible causes and identifying other possible contributing factors," the CDC said.</p><p>There has also been an increase in cases of pediatric hepatitis without a known cause recently reported in Europe and the CDC said it "has been in contact with our European counterparts to understand what they are learning."</p><div class="b-banner m-mobile-rectangle" data-position="mobile_rectangle" data-testid="mobile_rectangle" js-banner=""></div>
<p>Adenovirus has been confirmed in several of the European cases, but not all, the CDC said.</p><p>Symptoms of hepatitis, or inflammation of the liver, include:</p><ul><li>fever,&nbsp;</li><li>fatigue,&nbsp;</li><li>loss of appetite,&nbsp;</li><li>nausea,&nbsp;</li><li>vomiting,&nbsp;</li><li>abdominal pain,&nbsp;</li><li>dark urine,&nbsp;</li><li>light-colored stools,&nbsp;</li><li>joint pain,</li><li>jaundice</li></ul><p>Adenoviruses spread from person-to-person and most commonly cause respiratory illness, but depending on the type, can also cause other illnesses such as gastroenteritis (inflammation of the stomach or intestines), conjunctivitis (pink eye), and cystitis (bladder infection).&nbsp;</p><p>Adenovirus type 41 typically presents as diarrhea, vomiting and fever, often accompanied by respiratory symptoms.&nbsp;</p><div class="e-nativo-container" js-nativo=""></div><p>CDC is asking physicians to consider adenovirus testing for pediatric patients with hepatitis of unknown etiology, and to report any possible cases of hepatitis of unknown origin to CDC and state public health authorities.</p><div class="b-banner m-mobile-rectangle" data-position="mobile_rectangle" data-testid="mobile_rectangle" js-banner=""></div>
<p>"In addition, we encourage parents and caregivers to be aware of the symptoms of hepatitis, and to contact their healthcare provider with any concerns," the CDC said.&nbsp;</p><p>The CDC said it's also recommending children be up to date on all their vaccinations, and that "parents and caregivers of young children take the same everyday preventive actions that we recommend for everyone," including:</p><ul><li>Washing hands often,&nbsp;</li><li>Avoiding people who are sick,&nbsp;</li><li>Covering coughs and sneezes,&nbsp;</li><li>Avoiding touching the eyes, nose or mouth.&nbsp;</li></ul><p><a href="https://emergency.cdc.gov/han/2022/han00462.asp" target="_blank">Click here to read the CDC alert.</a></p>
        

        

        

        

        
          <p class="e-click-here-follow-btn" data-testid="bottom-paragraph">

            to follow Daily Voice
            
              Somers
            
            and receive free news updates.
          </p>
        
      </div>

      
    </section>

  <script>
    (function () {
      var bucket_storage_key = 'dv_instream_ad_system_bucket_8';
      var stored = localStorage.getItem(bucket_storage_key);

      // Default (localstorage or random)
      if (!!stored) {
        window.instream_ad_system = stored;
      }
      
      else {
        let random_val = Math.random()
        if (random_val < 0.4) {
          window.instream_ad_system = 'connatix';
        }
        else if (random_val < 0.5) {
          window.instream_ad_system = 'primis';
        }
        else {
          window.instream_ad_system = 'exco';
        }
      }

      // URL overrides
      if (window.location.search.indexOf('ads=connatix') > -1) {
        window.instream_ad_system = 'connatix';
      } else if (window.location.search.indexOf('ads=exco') > -1) {
        window.instream_ad_system = 'exco';
      } else if (window.location.search.indexOf('ads=primis') > -1) {
        window.instream_ad_system = 'primis';
      }

      localStorage.setItem(bucket_storage_key, window.instream_ad_system);

      /**
       * Since the video player on the page can be provided from one of multiple platforms (EX.CO, Connatix, etc.), 
       *    this requires different approaches to how we initialize the video player SDKs.
       * 
       * - Connatix Javascript SDK has to be initialized BEFORE the player id is inserted, because the player itself
       *    has to use the "window.cnx" object to initialize.
       * - EX.CO Javascript SDK, however, needs to be initialized AFTER the player id is inserted,
       *    because it scans the current page html for element with the target id and inserts the player into it.
       * - PRIMIS Inserts the player next to wherever the script is inserted, so it doesn't make sense
       *    to put it in the header.
       */
      const initExcoJsSdk = () => {
        (function(d,s,n){var js,fjs=d.getElementsByTagName(s)[0];js=d.createElement(s);js.className=n;js.src="//player.ex.co/player/994f6394-260b-4713-a0d7-0837545bba4a";fjs.parentNode.insertBefore(js,fjs);}(document,"script","exco-player"));
      }
      const initCnxJsSdk = () => {
        !function(n){if(!window.cnx){window.cnx={},window.cnx.cmd=[];var t=n.createElement('iframe');t.src='javascript:false'; t.display='none',t.onload=function(){var n=t.contentWindow.document,c=n.createElement('script');c.src='//cd.connatix.com/connatix.player.js?cid=ef8d6345-3814-451d-bee1-fda917851174',c.setAttribute('async','1'),c.setAttribute('type','text/javascript'),n.body.appendChild(c)},n.head.appendChild(t)}}(document);
      }
      document.addEventListener('insert-exco-sdk-script', () => initExcoJsSdk());
      document.addEventListener('insert-cnx-sdk-script', () => initCnxJsSdk());

      if (window.instream_ad_system === 'connatix') {
        initCnxJsSdk()
      }
      else if(window.instream_ad_system === 'exco') {
        const excoPlayerScriptId = '994f6394-260b-4713-a0d7-0837545bba4a';
        if (document.getElementById(excoPlayerScriptId)) {
          initExcoJsSdk();
        }
      }
      else if (window.instream_ad_system === 'primis') {
        // do nothing
      }
    })();
  </script>
